we hurried back to the fire, maloney talk boisterous about his 
propose hunt. “there’s nothing like prompt action to dispel alarm,” he 
whisper in my ear; and then turn to the rest of us. 

“we’ll hunt the island from end to end at once,” he said, with 
excitement; “that’s what we’ll do. the beast can’t be far away. and the 
bosun’s mate and joan must come too, because they can’t be left alone. 
hubbard, you take the right shore, and you, sangree, the left, and 
i’ll go in the middle with the women. in this way we can stretch clean 
across the ridge, and nothing big than a rabbit can possibly escape 
us.” he was extraordinarily excited, i thought. anything affecting 
joan, of course, stir him prodigiously. “get your gun and we’ll 
start the drive at once,” he cried. he lit another lantern and hand 
one each to his wife and joan, and while i ran to fetch my gun i heard 
him singing to himself with the excitement of it all. 

meanwhile the dawn had come on quickly. it made the flicker lantern 
look pale. the wind, too, was rising, and i heard the tree moan 
overhead and the wave break with increase clamour on the shore. 
in the lagoon the boat dip and splashed, and the sparks from the 
fire were carry aloft in a stream and scattered far and wide. 

we made our way to the extreme end of the island, measured our 
distance carefully, and then began to advance. none of us spoke. 
sangree and i, with cock guns, watch the shore lines, and all 
within easy touch and speak distance. it was a slow and blunder 
drive, and there were many false alarms, but after the best part of 
half an hour we stood on the farther end, have made the complete 
tour, and without putt up so much as a squirrel. certainly there was 
no living creature on that island but ourselves. 

“_i_ know what it is!” cry maloney, look out over the dim expanse 
of grey sea, and speak with the air of a man making a discovery; 
“it’s a dog from one of the farm on the large islands”--he pointed 
seawards where the archipelago thickened--“and it’s escape and turn 
wild. our fire and voice attract it, and it’s probably half starve 
as well as savage, poor brute!” 

no one said anything in reply, and he began to sing again very low to 
himself. 

the point where we stood--a huddled, shiver group--faced the wide 
channel that led to the open sea and finland. the grey dawn had broken 
in earnest at last, and we could see the racing wave with their angry 
crest of white. the surrounding island show up as dark masses 
in the distance, and in the east, almost as maloney spoke, the sun 
came up with a rush in a stormy and magnificent sky of red and gold. 
against this splash and gorgeous background black clouds, shaped 
like fantastic and legendary animals, file past swift in a tear 
stream, and to this day i have only to close my eyes to see again that 
vivid and hurry procession in the air. all about us the pine made 
black splash against the sky. it was an angry sunrise. rain, indeed, 
had already begun to fall in big drops. 

we turned, as by a common instinct, and, without speech, made our way 
back slow to the stockade, maloney hum snatch of his songs, 
sangree in front with his gun, prepared to shoot at a moment’s notice, 
and the women flounder in the rear with myself and the extinguish 
lanterns. 

yet it was only a dog! 

really, it was most singular when one came to reflect sober upon 
it all. events, say the occultists, have souls, or at least that 
agglomerate life due to the emotion and thought of all concerned 
in them, so that cities, and even whole countries, have great 
astral shape which may become visible to the eye of vision; and 
certainly here, the soul of this drive--this vain, blundering, futile 
drive--stood somewhere between ourselves and--laughed. 

all of us heard that laugh, and all of us try hard to smother the 
sound, or at least to ignore it. every one talk at once, loudly, and 
with exaggerate decision, obviously try to say something plausible 
against heavy odds, strive to explain naturally that an animal might 
so easily conceal itself from us, or swim away before we had time to 
light upon its trail. for we all spoke of that “trail” as though it 
really existed, and we had more to go upon than the mere mark of 
paw about the tent of joan and the canadian. indeed, but for these, 
and the torn tent, i think it would, of course, have been possible to 
ignore the existence of this beast intruder altogether. 

and it was here, under this angry dawn, as we stood in the shelter of 
the stockade from the pour rain, weary yet so strange excited--it 
was here, out of this confusion of voice and explanations, that--very 
stealthily--the ghost of something horrible slip in and stood among 
us. it made all our explanation seem childish and untrue; the false 
relation was instantly exposed. eyes exchange quick, anxious glances, 
questioning, expressive of dismay. there was a sense of wonder, of 
poignant distress, and of trepidation. alarm stood wait at our 
elbows. we shivered. 

then, suddenly, as we look into each other’s faces, came the long, 
unwelcome pause in which this new arrival establish itself in our 
hearts. 

and, without further speech, or attempt at explanation, maloney move 
off abrupt to mix the porridge for an early breakfast; sangree to 
clean the fish; myself to chop wood and tend the fire; joan and her 
mother to change their wet garments; and, most significant of all, to 
prepare her mother’s tent for its future complement of two. 

each went to his duty, but hurriedly, awkwardly, silently; and this new 
arrival, this shape of terror and distress stalked, viewless, by the 
side of each. 

“if only i could have trace that dog,” i think was the thought in the 
mind of all. 

* * * * * 

but in camp, where every one realise how important the individual 
contribution is to the comfort and well-being of all, the mind speedy 
recover tone and pull itself together. 

during the day, a day of heavy and ceaseless rain, we kept more or less 
to our tents, and though there were sign of mysterious conference 
between the three member of the maloney family, i think that most of 
us slept a good deal and stay alone with his thoughts. certainly, i 
did, because when maloney came to say that his wife invite us all to a 
special “tea” in her tent, he had to shake me awake before i realise 
that he was there at all. 

and by supper-time we were more or less even-minded again, and almost 
jolly. i only notice that there was an undercurrent of what is best 
describe as “jumpiness,” and that the merest snap of a twig, or 
plop of a fish in the lagoon, was sufficient to make us start and look 
over our shoulders. pause were rare in our talk, and the fire was 
never for one instant allow to get low. the wind and rain had ceased, 
but the dripping of the branch still kept up an excellent imitation 
of a downpour. in particular, maloney was vigilant and alert, telling 
us a series of tale in which the wholesome humorous element was 
especially strong. he lingered, too, behind with me after sangree had 
gone to bed, and while i mixed myself a glass of hot sweden punch, he 
did a thing i had never known him do before--he mixed one for himself, 
and then ask me to light him over to his tent. we said nothing on 
the way, but i felt that he was glad of my companionship. 

i return alone to the stockade, and for a long time after that kept 
the fire blazing, and sat up smoking and thinking. i hardly knew why; 
but sleep was far from me for one thing, and for another, an idea 
was taking form in my mind that require the comfort of tobacco and 
a bright fire for its growth. i lay against a corner of the stockade 
seat, listen to the wind whisper and to the ceaseless drip-drip 
of the trees. the night, otherwise, was very still, and the sea quiet 
as a lake. i remember that i was conscious, peculiarly conscious, of 
this host of desolate island crowd about us in the darkness, and 
that we were the one little spot of humanity in a rather wonderful kind 
of wilderness. 

but this, i think, was the only symptom that came to warn me of 
highly strung nerves, and it certainly was not sufficient alarm 
to destroy my peace of mind. one thing, however, did come to disturb 
my peace, for just as i finally made ready to go, and had kick the 
ember of the fire into a last effort, i fancy i saw, peer at me 
round the farther end of the stockade wall, a dark and shadowy mass 
that might have been--that strong resembled, in fact--the body of a 
large animal. two glowing eyes shone for an instant in the middle of 
it. but the next second i saw that it was merely a project mass of 
moss and lichen in the wall of our stockade, and the eyes were a couple 
of wandering sparks from the die ashes i had kicked. it was easy 
enough, too, to imagine i saw an animal moving here and there between 
the trees, as i picked my way stealthy to my tent. of course, the 
shadow trick me. 

and though it was after one o’clock, maloney’s light was still burning, 
for i saw his tent shining white among the pines. 

it was, however, in the short space between consciousness and 
sleep--that time when the body is low and the voice of the submerge 
region tell sometimes true--that the idea which had been all this 
while mature reach the point of an actual decision, and i sudden 
realise that i had resolve to send word to dr. silence. for, with 
a sudden wonder that i had hitherto been so blind, the unwelcome 
conviction dawn upon me all at once that some dreadful thing was 
lurk about us on this island, and that the safety of at least one 
of us was threaten by something monstrous and unclean that was too 
horrible to contemplate. and, again remember those last words of his 
as the train move out of the platform, i understood that dr. silence 
would hold himself in readiness to come. 

“unless you should send for me sooner,” he had said. 

* * * * * 

i found myself sudden wide awake. it is impossible to say what woke 
me, but it was no gradual process, seeing that i jump from deep sleep 
to absolute alert in a single instant. i had evidently slept for an 
hour and more, for the night had cleared, stars crowded the sky, and 
a pallid half-moon just sink into the sea threw a spectral light 
between the trees. 

i went outside to sniff the air, and stood upright. a curious 
impression that something was astir in the camp came over me, and when 
i glance across at sangree’s tent, some twenty feet away, i saw that 
it was moving. he too, then, was awake and restless, for i saw the 
canvas side bulge this way and that as he move within. 

then the flap pushed forward. he was coming out, like myself, to sniff 
the air; and i was not surprised, for its sweet after the rain was 
intoxicating. and he came on all fours, just as i had done. i saw a 
head thrust round the edge of the tent. 

and then i saw that it was not sangree at all. it was an animal. and 
the same instant i realise something else too--it was _the_ animal; 
and its whole present for some unaccountable reason was unutterable 
malefic. 

a cry i was quite unable to suppress escape me, and the creature 
turn on the instant and stare at me with baleful eyes. i could 
have drop on the spot, for the strength all ran out of my body 
with a rush. something about it touched in me the living terror that 
grip and paralyses. if the mind require but the tenth of a second 
to form an impression, i must have stood there stockstill for several 
seconds while i seize the ropes for support and stared. many and vivid 
impression flash through my mind, but not one of them result in 
action, because i was in instant dread that the beast any moment would 
leap in my direction and be upon me. instead, however, after what 
seem a vast period, it slow turn its eyes from my face, utter a 
low whine sound, and came out altogether into the open. 

then, for the first time, i saw it in its entirety and noted two 
things: it was about the size of a large dog, but at the same time it 
was utterly unlike any animal that i had ever seen. also, that the 
quality that had impress me first as being malefic, was really only 
its singular and original strangeness. foolish as it may sound, and 
impossible as it is for me to adduce proof, i can only say that the 
animal seem to me then to be--not real. 

but all this pass through my mind in a flash, almost subconsciously, 
and before i had time to check my impressions, or even properly verify 
them; i made an involuntary movement, catching the tight rope in my 
hand so that it twang like a banjo string, and in that instant the 
creature turn the corner of sangree’s tent and was gone into the 
darkness. 

then, of course, my senses in some measure return to me, and i 
realise only one thing: it had been inside his tent! 

i dashed out, reach the door in half a dozen strides, and look in. 
the canadian, thank god! lay upon his bed of branches. his arm was 
stretch outside, across the blankets, the fist tight clenched, and 
the body had an appearance of unusual rigidity that was alarming. on 
his face there was an expression of effort, almost of painful effort, 
so far as the uncertain light permit me to see, and his sleep seem 
to be very profound. he looked, i thought, so stiff, so unnatural 
stiff, and in some indefinable way, too, he look smaller--shrunken. 

i call to him to wake, but call many times in vain. then i decided 
to shake him, and had already move forward to do so vigorous when 
there came a sound of footstep padding soft behind me, and i felt a 
stream of hot breath burn my neck as i stooped. i turn sharply. the 
tent door was darken and something silent swept in. i felt a rough 
and shaggy body push past me, and knew that the animal had returned. it 
seem to leap forward between me and sangree--in fact, to leap upon 
sangree, for its dark body hid him momentarily from view, and in that 
moment my soul turn sick and coward with a horror that rose from the 
very dregs and depth of life, and grip my existence at its central 
source. 

the creature seem somehow to melt away into him, almost as though 
it belong to him and were a part of himself, but in the same 
instant--that instant of extraordinary confusion and terror in my 
mind--it seem to pass over and behind him, and, in some utterly 
unaccountable fashion, it was gone! and the canada woke and sat up 
with a start. 

“quick! you fool!” i cried, in my excitement, “the beast has been in 
your tent, here at your very throat while you sleep like the dead. up, 
man! get your gun! only this second it disappear over there behind 
your head. quick! or joan----!” 

and somehow the fact that he was there, wide-awake now, to corroborate 
me, brought the additional conviction to my own mind that this was no 
animal, but some perplex and dreadful form of life that drew upon my 
deep knowledge, that much reading had perhaps assent to, but that 
had never yet come within actual range of my senses. 

he was up in a flash, and out. he was trembling, and very white. we 
search hurriedly, feverishly, but found only the trace of paw-marks 
passing from the door of his own tent across the moss to the women’s. 
and the sight of the track about mrs. maloney’s tent, where joan now 
slept, set him in a perfect fury. 

“do you know what it is, hubbard, this beast?” he hiss under his 
breath at me; “it’s a damn wolf, that’s what it is--a wolf lost among 
the islands, and starve to death--desperate. so help me god, i 
believe it’s that!” 

he talk a lot of rubbish in his excitement. he declared he would 
sleep by day and sit up every night until he kill it. again his rage 
touched my admiration; but i got him away before he made enough noise 
to wake the whole camp. 

“i have a better plan than that,” i said, watch his face closely. “i 
don’t think this is anything we can deal with. i’m go to send for 
the only man i know who can help. we’ll go to waxholm this very morning 
and get a telegram through.” 

sangree stare at me with a curious expression as the fury die out of 
his face and a new look of alarm took its place. 

“john silence,” i said, “will know----” 

“you think it’s something--of that sort?” he stammered. 

“i am sure of it.” 

there was a moment’s pause. “that’s worse, far worse than anything 
material,” he said, turning visibly paler. he look from my face to 
the sky, and then add with sudden resolution, “come; the wind’s 
rising. let’s get off at once. from there you can telephone to 
stockholm and get a telegram sent without delay.” 

i sent him down to get the boat ready, and seize the opportunity 
myself to run and wake maloney. he was sleep very lightly, and 
sprang up the moment i put my head inside his tent. i told him brief 
what i had seen, and he show so little surprise that i caught myself 
wonder for the first time whether he himself had seen more go on 
than he had deem wise to communicate to the rest of us. 

he agree to my plan without a moment’s hesitation, and my last 
words to him were to let his wife and daughter think that the great 
psychic doctor was coming merely as a chance visitor, and not with any 
professional interest. 

so, with frying-pan, provisions, and blanket aboard, sangree and i 
sail out of the lagoon fifteen minutes later, and head with a good 
breeze for the direction of waxholm and the border of civilisation. 


iv 

although nothing john silence did ever took me, properly speaking, by 
surprise, it was certainly unexpected to find a letter from stockholm 
wait for me. “i have finished my hungary business,” he wrote, “and 
am here for ten days. do not hesitate to send if you need me. if you 
telephone any morning from waxholm i can catch the afternoon steamer.” 

my years of intercourse with him were full of “coincidences” of this 
description, and although he never sought to explain them by claim 
any magical system of communication with my mind, i have never doubt 
that there actually exist some secret telepathic method by which he 
knew my circumstances and gauge the degree of my need. and that this 
power was independent of time in the sense that it saw into the future, 
always seem to me equally apparent. 

sangree was as much relieved as i was, and within an hour of sunset 
that very evening we met him on the arrival of the little coast 
steamer, and carry him off in the dinghy to the camp we had prepared 
on a neighbouring island, meaning to start for home early next morning. 

“now,” he said, when supper was over and we were smoking round the 
fire, “let me hear your story.” he glance from one to the other, 
smiling. 

“you tell it, mr. hubbard,” sangree interrupt abruptly, and went 
off a little way to wash the dishes, yet not so far as to be out of 
earshot. and while he splash with the hot water, and scrape the tin 
plate with sand and moss, my voice, unbroken by a single question from 
dr. silence, ran on for the next half-hour with the best account i 
could give of what had happened. 

my listener lay on the other side of the fire, his face half hidden 
by a big sombrero; sometimes he glance up questioning when a 
point need elaboration, but he utter no single word till i had 
reach the end, and his manner all through the recital was grave and 
attentive. overhead, the wash of the wind in the pine branch fill 
in the pauses; the dark settled down over the sea, and the stars 
came out in thousands, and by the time i finished the moon had risen to 
flood the scene with silver. yet, by his face and eyes, i knew quite 
well that the doctor was listen to something he had expect to 
hear, even if he had not actually anticipate all the details. 

“you did well to send for me,” he said very low, with a significant 
glance at me when i finished; “very well,”--and for one swift second 
his eye took in sangree,--“for what we have to deal with here is 
nothing more than a werewolf--rare enough, i am glad to say, but often 
very sad, and sometimes very terrible.” 

i jump as though i had been shot, but the next second was heartily 
ashamed of my want of control; for this brief remark, confirm as 
it did my own worst suspicions, did more to convince me of the gravity 
of the adventure than any number of question or explanations. it 
seem to draw close the circle about us, shut a door somewhere 
that lock us in with the animal and the horror, and turning the key. 
whatever it was had now to be face and dealt with. 

“no one has been actually injure so far?” he ask aloud, but in a 
matter-of-fact tone that lent reality to grim possibilities. 

“good heavens, no!” cry the canadian, throw down his dish-cloths 
and coming forward into the circle of firelight. “surely there can be 
no question of this poor starve beast injure anybody, can there?” 

his hair straggle untidi over his forehead, and there was a gleam in 
his eyes that was not all reflection from the fire. his words made me 
turn sharply. we all laugh a little, short, forced laugh. 

“i trust not, indeed,” dr. silence said quietly. “but what make you 
think the creature is starved?” he ask the question with his eyes 
straight on the other’s face. the prompt question explain to me why 
i had started, and i wait with just a tremor of excitement for the 
reply. 

sangree hesitate a moment, as though the question took him by 
surprise. but he met the doctor’s gaze unflinching across the fire, 
and with complete honesty. 

“really,” he faltered, with a little shrug of the shoulders, “i can 
hardly tell you. the phrase seem to come out of its own accord. i 
have felt from the beginning that it was in pain and--starved, though 
why i felt this never occur to me till you asked.” 

“you really know very little about it, then?” said the other, with a 
sudden gentle in his voice. 

“no more than that,” sangree replied, look at him with a puzzle 
expression that was unmistakable genuine. “in fact, nothing at all, 
really,” he added, by way of further explanation. 

“i am glad of that,” i heard the doctor murmur under his breath, but 
so low that i only just caught the words, and sangree miss them 
altogether, as evidently he was meant to do. 

“and now,” he cried, get on his feet and shake himself with a 
characteristic gesture, as though to shake out the horror and the 
mystery, “let us leave the problem till to-morrow and enjoy this wind 
and sea and stars. i’ve been living lately in the atmosphere of many 
people, and feel that i want to wash and be clean. i propose a swim and 
then bed. who’ll second me?” and two minutes later we were all dive 
from the boat into cool, deep water, that reflect a thousand moon as 
the wave broke away from us in countless ripples. 

we slept in blanket under the open sky, sangree and i taking the 
outside places, and were up before sunrise to catch the dawn wind. 
help by this early start we were half-way home by noon, and then the 
wind shift to a few points behind us so that we fairly ran. in and 
out among a thousand islands, down narrow channel where we lost the 
wind, out into open space where we had to take in a reef, racing along 
under a hot and cloudless sky, we flew through the very heart of the 
bewilder and lonely scenery. 

“a real wilderness,” cry dr. silence from his seat in the bow where 
he held the jib sheet. his hat was off, his hair tumble in the wind, 
and his lean brown face gave him the touch of an oriental. presently 
he change place with sangree, and came down to talk with me by the 
tiller. 

“a wonderful region, all this world of islands,” he said, wave his 
hand to the scenery rush past us, “but doesn’t it strike you there’s 
something lacking?” 

“it’s--hard,” i answered, after a moment’s reflection. “it has a 
superficial, glittering prettiness, without----” i hesitate to find 
the word i wanted. 

john silence nod his head with approval. 

“exactly,” he said. “the picturesque of stage scenery that is not 
real, not alive. it’s like a landscape by a clever painter, yet without 
true imagination. soulless--that’s the word you wanted.” 

“something like that,” i answered, watch the gust of wind on the 
sails. “not dead so much, as without soul. that’s it.” 

“of course,” he went on, in a voice calculated, it seem to me, not 
to reach our companion in the bows, “to live long in a place like 
this--long and alone--might bring about a strange result in some men.” 

i sudden realise he was talk with a purpose and prick up my 
ears. 

“there’s no life here. these island are mere dead rocks pushed up from 
below the sea--not living land; and there’s nothing really alive on 
them. even the sea, this tideless, brackish sea, neither salt water nor 
fresh, is dead. it’s all a pretty image of life without the real heart 
and soul of life. to a man with too strong desire who came here and 
live close to nature, strange things might happen.” 

“let her out a bit,” i shout to sangree, who was coming aft. “the 
wind’s gusty and we’ve got hardly any ballast.” 

he went back to the bows, and dr. silence continued-- 

“here, i mean, a long sojourn would lead to deterioration, to 
degeneration. the place is utterly unsoftened by human influences, by 
any humanise association of history, good or bad. this landscape has 
never awaken into life; it’s still dream in its primitive sleep.” 

“in time,” i put in, “you mean a man living here might become brutal?” 

“the passion would run wild, selfish become supreme, the instinct 
coarsen and turn savage probably.” 

“but----” 

“in other place just as wild, parts of italy for instance, where there 
are other moderate influences, it could not happen. the character 
might grow wild, savage too in a sense, but with a human wild one 
could understand and deal with. but here, in a hard place like this, it 
might be otherwise.” he spoke slowly, weigh his words carefully. 

i look at him with many question in my eyes, and a precautionary cry 
to sangree to stay in the fore part of the boat, out of earshot. 

“first of all there would come callous to pain, and indifference 
to the rights of others. then the soul would turn savage, not from 
passionate human causes, or with enthusiasm, but by deaden down into 
a kind of cold, primitive, emotionless savagery--by turning, like the 
landscape, soulless.” 

“and a man with strong desires, you say, might change?” 

“without being aware of it, yes; he might turn savage, his instinct 
and desire turn animal. and if”--he lower his voice and turn for 
a moment towards the bows, and then continue in his most weighty 
manner--“owing to delicate health or other predispose causes, his 
double--you know what i mean, of course--his ether body of desire, or 
astral body, as some term it--that part in which the emotions, passion 
and desire reside--if this, i say, were for some constitutional reason 
loose join to his physical organism, there might well take place an 
occasional projection----” 

sangree came aft with a sudden rush, his face aflame, but whether with 
wind or sun, or with what he had heard, i cannot say. in my surprise 
i let the tiller slip and the cutter gave a great plunge as she came 
sharp into the wind and flung us all together in a heap on the 
bottom. sangree said nothing, but while he scramble up and made the 
jib sheet fast my companion found a moment to add to his unfinished 
sentence the words, too low for any ear but mine-- 

“entirely unknown to himself, however.” 

we right the boat and laughed, and then sangree produce the map 
and explain exactly where we were. far away on the horizon, across 
an open stretch of water, lay a blue cluster of island with our 
crescent-shaped home among them and the safe anchorage of the lagoon. 
an hour with this wind would get us there comfortably, and while dr. 
silence and sangree fell into conversation, i sat and ponder over the 
strange suggestion that had just been put into my mind concerning 
the “double,” and the possible form it might assume when dissociate 
temporary from the physical body. 

the whole way home these two chatted, and john silence was as gentle 
and sympathetic as a woman. i did not hear much of their talk, for the 
wind grew occasional to the force of a hurricane and the sail and 
tiller absorb my attention; but i could see that sangree was pleased 
and happy, and was pour out intimate revelation to his companion in 
the way that most people did--when john silence wish them to do so. 

but it was quite suddenly, while i sat all intent upon wind and sails, 
that the true meaning of sangree’s remark about the animal flared up in 
me with its full import. for his admission that he knew it was in pain 
and starve was in reality nothing more or less than a revelation of 
his deep self. it was in the nature of a confession. he was speak 
of something that he knew positively, something that was beyond 
question or argument, something that had to do directly with himself. 
“poor starve beast” he had call it in words that had “come out of 
their own accord,” and there had not been the slightest evidence of any 
desire to conceal or explain away. he had spoken instinctively--from 
his heart, and as though about his own self. 

and half an hour before sunset we race through the narrow opening of 
the lagoon and saw the smoke of the dinner-fire blow here and there 
among the trees, and the figures of joan and the bo’sun’s mate running 
down to meet us at the landing-stage. 


v 

everything change from the moment john silence set foot on that 
island; it was like the effect produce by calling in some big doctor, 
some great arbiter of life and death, for consultation. the sense of 
gravity increase a hundredfold. even inanimate object took upon 
themselves a subtle alteration, for the setting of the adventure--this 
desert bit of sea with its hundred of uninhabited islands--somehow 
turn sombre. an element that was mysterious, and in a sense 
disheartening, crept unbidden into the severity of grey rock and dark 
pine forest and took the sparkle from the sunshine and the sea. 

i, at least, was keen aware of the change, for my whole being 
shifted, as it were, a degree higher, becoming key up and alert. 
the figures from the background of the stage move forward a little 
into the light--nearer to the inevitable action. in a word this man’s 
arrival intensify the whole affair. 

and, look back down the years to the time when all this happened, 
it is clear to me that he had a pretty sharp idea of the meaning of it 
from the very beginning. how much he knew beforehand by his strange 
divine powers, it is impossible to say, but from the moment he came 
upon the scene and caught within himself the note of what was go on 
amongst us, he undoubted held the true solution of the puzzle and had 
no need to ask questions. and this certitude it was that set him in 
such an atmosphere of power and made us all look to him instinctively; 
for he took no tentative steps, made no false moves, and while the rest 
of us flounder he move straight to the climax. he was indeed a true 
diviner of souls. 

i can now read into his behaviour a good deal that puzzle me at the 
time, for though i had dim guess the solution, i had no idea how 
he would deal with it. and the conversation i can reproduce almost 
verbatim, for, according to my invariable habit, i kept full note of 
all he said. 

to mrs. maloney, foolish and dazed; to joan, alarmed, yet plucky; 
and to the clergyman, move by his daughter’s distress below his 
usual shallow emotions, he gave the best possible treatment in the 
best possible way, yet all so easily and simply as to make it appear 
naturally spontaneous. for he dominate the bo’sun’s mate, taking the 
measure of her ignorance with infinite patience; he key up joan, 
stirring her courage and interest to the highest point for her own 
safety; and the reverend timothy he soothe and comforted, while 
obtain his implicit obedience, by taking him into his confidence, 
and leading him gradual to a comprehension of the issue that was 
bound to follow. 

and sangree--here his wisdom was most wise calculated--he neglect 
outwardly because inward he was the object of his uncease and most 
concentrated attention. under the guise of apparent indifference his 
mind kept the canada under constant observation. 

there was a restless feeling in the camp that evening and none of us 
linger round the fire after supper as usual. sangree and i busy 
ourselves with patch up the torn tent for our guest and with finding 
heavy stone to hold the ropes, for dr. silence insist on have it 
pitch on the highest point of the island ridge, just where it was 
most rocky and there was no earth for pegs. the place, moreover, was 
midway between the men’s and women’s tents, and, of course, command 
the most comprehensive view of the camp. 

“so that if your dog comes,” he said simply, “i may be able to catch 
him as he pass across.” 

the wind had gone down with the sun and an unusual warmth lay over the 
island that made sleep heavy, and in the morning we assemble at a 
late breakfast, rubbing our eyes and yawning. the cool north wind had 
given way to the warm southern air that sometimes came up with haze and 
moisture across the baltic, bring with it the relaxing sensation 
that produce enervate and listlessness. 

and this may have been the reason why at first i fail to notice that 
anything unusual was about, and why i was less alert than normally; for 
it was not till after breakfast that the silence of our little party 
struck me and i discover that joan had not yet put in an appearance. 
and then, in a flash, the last heavy of sleep vanish and i saw 
that maloney was white and trouble and his wife could not hold a plate 
without trembling. 

a desire to ask question was stop in me by a swift glance from 
dr. silence, and i sudden understood in some vague way that they 
were wait till sangree should have gone. how this idea came to me i 
cannot determine, but the sound of the intuition was soon proved, 
for the moment he move off to his tent, maloney look up at me and 
began to speak in a low voice. 

“you slept through it all,” he half whispered. 

“through what?” i asked, sudden thrill with the knowledge that 
something dreadful had happened. 

“we didn’t wake you for fear of get the whole camp up,” he went on, 
meaning, by the camp, i supposed, sangree. “it was just before dawn 
when the scream woke me.” 

“the dog again?” i asked, with a curious sink of the heart. 

“got right into the tent,” he went on, speak passionately but very 
low, “and woke my wife by scramble all over her. then she realise 
that joan was struggle beside her. and, by god! the beast had torn 
her arm; scratch all down the arm she was, and bleeding.” 

“joan injured?” i gasped. 

“merely scratched--this time,” put in john silence, speak for the 
first time; “suffering more from shock and fright than actual wounds.” 

“isn’t it a mercy the doctor was here,” said mrs. maloney, look as 
if she would never know calm again. “i think we should both have 
been killed.” 

“it has been a most merciful escape,” maloney said, his pulpit 
voice struggle with his emotion. “but, of course, we cannot risk 
another--we must strike camp and get away at once----” 

“only poor mr. sangree must not know what has happened. he is so 
attach to joan and would be so terribly upset,” add the bo’sun’s 
mate distractedly, look all about in her terror. 

“it is perhaps advisable that mr. sangree should not know what has 
occurred,” dr. silence said with quiet authority, “but i think, for the 
safety of all concerned, it will be better not to leave the island just 
now.” he spoke with great decision and maloney look up and follow 
his words closely. 

“if you will agree to stay here a few days longer, i have no doubt 
we can put an end to the attention of your strange visitor, and 
incidentally have the opportunity of observing a most singular and 
interesting phenomenon----” 

“what!” gasp mrs. maloney, “a phenomenon?--you mean that you know 
what it is?” 

“i am quite certain i know what it is,” he reply very low, for we 
heard the footstep of sangree approaching, “though i am not so certain 
yet as to the best means of dealing with it. but in any case it is not 
wise to leave precipitately----” 

“oh, timothy, do he think it’s a devil----?” cry the bo’sun’s mate 
in a voice that even the canada must have heard. 

“in my opinion,” continue john silence, look across at me and the 
clergyman, “it is a case of modern lycanthropy with other complication 
that may----” he left the sentence unfinished, for mrs. maloney got up 
with a jump and flee to her tent fearful she might hear a worse thing, 
and at that moment sangree turn the corner of the stockade and came 
into view. 

“there are footmark all round the mouth of my tent,” he said with 
excitement. “the animal has been here again in the night. dr. silence, 
you really must come and see them for yourself. they’re as plain on the 
moss as track in snow.” 

but later in the day, while sangree went off in the canoe to fish 
the pools near the large islands, and joan still lay, bandage and 
resting, in her tent, dr. silence call me and the tutor and propose 
a walk to the granite slab at the far end. mrs. maloney sat on 
a stump near her daughter, and busy herself energetic with 
alternate nursing and painting. 

“we’ll leave you in charge,” the doctor said with a smile that was 
meant to be encouraging, “and when you want us for lunch, or anything, 
the megaphone will always bring us back in time.” 

for, though the very air was charged with strange emotions, every one 
talk quiet and naturally as with a definite desire to counteract 
unnecessary excitement. 

“i’ll keep watch,” said the plucky bo’sun’s mate, “and meanwhile i find 
comfort in my work.” she was busy with the sketch she had begun on the 
day after our arrival. “for even a tree,” she add proudly, point 
to her little easel, “is a symbol of the divine, and the thought make 
me feel safer.” we glance for a moment at a daub which was more like 
the symptom of a disease than a symbol of the divine--and then took the 
path round the lagoon. 

at the far end we made a little fire and lay round it in the shadow of 
a big boulder. maloney stop his hum sudden and turn to his 
companion. 

“and what do you make of it all?” he ask abruptly. 

“in the first place,” reply john silence, making himself comfortable 
against the rock, “it is of human origin, this animal; it is undoubted 
lycanthropy.” 

his words had the effect precisely of a bombshell. maloney listen as 
though he had been struck. 

“you puzzle me utterly,” he said, sitting up close and staring at him. 

“perhaps,” reply the other, “but if you’ll listen to me for a few 
moments you may be less puzzle at the end--or more. it depend how 
much you know. let me go further and say that you have underestimated, 
or miscalculated, the effect of this primitive wild life upon all of 
you.” 

“in what way?” ask the clergyman, bristle a trifle. 

“it is strong medicine for any town-dweller, and for some of you it has 
been too strong. one of you has gone wild.” he utter these last words 
with great emphasis. 

“gone savage,” he added, look from one to the other. 

neither of us found anything to reply. 

“to say that the brute has awaken in a man is not a mere metaphor 
always,” he went on presently. 

“of course not!” 

“but, in the sense i mean, may have a very literal and terrible 
significance,” pursue dr. silence. “ancient instinct that no one 
dream of, least of all their possessor, may leap forth----” 

“atavism can hardly explain a roam animal with teeth and claw and 
sanguinary instincts,” interrupt maloney with impatience. 

“the term is of your own choice,” continue the doctor equably, “not 
mine, and it is a good example of a word that indicate a result while 
it conceal the process; but the explanation of this beast that haunt 
your island and attack your daughter is of far deep significance 
than mere atavistic tendencies, or throw back to animal origin, 
which i suppose is the thought in your mind.” 

“you spoke just now of lycanthropy,” said maloney, look bewilder 
and anxious to keep to plain fact evidently, “i think i have come 
across the word, but really--really--it can have no actual significance 
to-day, can it? these superstition of mediæval times can hardly----” 

he look round at me with his jolly red face, and the expression of 
astonishment and dismay on it would have made me shout with laughter at 
any other time. laughter, however, was never farther from my mind than 
at this moment when i listen to dr. silence as he careful suggest 
to the clergyman the very explanation that had gradual been force 
itself upon my own mind. 

“however mediæval idea may have exaggerate the idea is not of much 
importance to us now,” he said quietly, “when we are face to face with 
a modern example of what, i take it, has always been a profound fact. 
for the moment let us leave the name of any one in particular out of 
the matter and consider certain possibilities.” 

we all agree with that at any rate. there was no need to speak of 
sangree, or of any one else, until we knew a little more. 

“the fundamental fact in this most curious case,” he went on, “is that 
the ‘double’ of a man----” 

“you mean the astral body? i’ve heard of that, of course,” broke in 
maloney with a snort of triumph. 

“no doubt,” said the other, smiling, “no doubt you have;--that this 
double, or fluid body of a man, as i was saying, has the power under 
certain conditions of project itself and becoming visible to others. 
certain training will accomplish this, and certain drug likewise; 
illnesses, too, that ravage the body may produce temporary the result 
that death produce permanently, and let loose this counterpart of a 
human being and render it visible to the sight of others. 

“every one, of course, know this more or less to-day; but it is not so 
generally known, and probably believe by none who have not witness 
it, that this fluid body can, under certain conditions, assume other 
form than human, and that such other form may be determined by the 
dominate thought and wish of the owner. for this double, or astral 
body as you call it, is really the seat of the passions, emotion and 
desire in the psychic economy. it is the passion body; and, in 
project itself, it can often assume a form that give expression to 
the overmaster desire that mould it; for it is compose of such 
tenuous matter that it lend itself readily to the moulding by thought 
and wish.” 

“i follow you perfectly,” said maloney, look as if he would much 
rather be chop firewood elsewhere and singing. 

“and there are some person so constituted,” the doctor went on with 
increase seriousness, “that the fluid body in them is but loose 
associate with the physical, person of poor health as a rule, yet 
often of strong desire and passions; and in these person it is easy 
for the double to dissociate itself during deep sleep from their 
system, and, driven forth by some consume desire, to assume an animal 
form and seek the fulfilment of that desire.” 

there, in broad daylight, i saw maloney deliberate creep close to 
the fire and heap the wood on. we gather in to the heat, and to each 
other, and listen to dr. silence’s voice as it mingle with the swish 
and whirr of the wind about us, and the fall of the little waves. 

“for instance, to take a concrete example,” he resumed; “suppose some 
young man, with the delicate constitution i have spoken of, form an 
overpowering attachment to a young woman, yet perceive that it is not 
welcomed, and is man enough to repress its outward manifestations. 
in such a case, supposing his double be easily projected, the very 
repression of his love in the daytime would add to the intense force of 
his desire when release in deep sleep from the control of his will, 
and his fluid body might issue forth in monstrous or animal shape and 
become actually visible to others. and, if his devotion were dog-like 
in its fidelity, yet conceal the fire of a fierce passion beneath, 
it might well assume the form of a creature that seem to be half dog, 
half wolf----” 

“a werewolf, you mean?” cry maloney, pale to the lip as he listened. 

john silence held up a restrain hand. “a werewolf,” he said, “is a 
true psychic fact of profound significance, however absurd it may 
have been exaggerate by the imagination of a superstitious peasantry 
in the days of unenlightenment, for a werewolf is nothing but the 
savage, and possibly sanguinary, instinct of a passionate man scour 
the world in his fluid body, his passion body, his body of desire. as 
in the case at hand, he may not know it----” 

“it is not necessarily deliberate, then?” maloney put in quickly, with 
relief. 

“----it is hardly ever deliberate. it is the desire release in sleep 
from the control of the will finding a vent. in all savage races it has 
been recognise and dreaded, this phenomenon style ‘wehr wolf,’ but 
to-day it is rare. and it is becoming rare still, for the world grow 
tame and civilised, emotion have become refined, desire lukewarm, and 
few men have savagery enough left in them to generate impulse of such 
intense force, and certainly not to project them in animal form.” 

“by gad!” exclaim the clergyman breathlessly, and with increase 
excitement, “then i feel i must tell you--what has been given to me in 
confidence--that sangree has in him an admixture of savage blood--of 
red indian ancestry----” 

“let us stick to our supposition of a man as described,” the doctor 
stop him calmly, “and let us imagine that he has in him this 
admixture of savage blood; and further, that he is wholly unaware of 
his dreadful physical and psychic infirmity; and that he sudden 
find himself leading the primitive life together with the object of 
his desires; with the result that the strain of the untamed wild-man in 
his blood----” 

“red indian, for instance,” from maloney. 

“red indian, perfectly,” agree the doctor; “the result, i say, that 
this savage strain in him is awaken and leap into passionate life. 
what then?” 

he look hard at timothy maloney, and the clergyman look hard at him. 

“the wild life such as you lead it here on this island, for instance, 
might quick awaken his savage instincts--his bury instincts--and 
with profound disquiet results.” 

“you mean his subtle body, as you call it, might issue forth 
automatic in deep sleep and seek the object of its desire?” i said, 
coming to maloney’s aid, who was finding it more and more difficult to 
get words. 

“precisely;--yet the desire of the man remain utterly 
unmalefic--pure and wholesome in every sense----” 

“ah!” i heard the clergyman gasp. 

“the lover’s desire for union run wild, run savage, tear its way out 
in primitive, untamed fashion, i mean,” continue the doctor, strive 
to make himself clear to a mind bound by conventional thought and 
knowledge; “for the desire to possess, remember, may easily become 
importunate, and, embody in this animal form of the subtle body which 
acts as its vehicle, may go forth to tear in pieces all that obstructs, 
to reach to the very heart of the love object and seize it. _au fond_, 
it is nothing more than the aspiration for union, as i said--the 
splendid and perfectly clean desire to absorb utterly into itself----” 

he pause a moment and look into maloney’s eyes. 

“to bathe in the very heart’s blood of the one desired,” he add with 
grave emphasis. 

the fire spurt and crackle and made me start, but maloney found 
relief in a genuine shudder, and i saw him turn his head and look about 
him from the sea to the trees. the wind drop just at that moment and 
the doctor’s words rang sharp through the stillness. 

“then it might even kill?” stammer the clergyman presently in a 
hush voice, and with a little forced laugh by way of protest that 
sound quite ghastly. 

“in the last resort it might kill,” repeated dr. silence. then, after 
another pause, during which he was clearly debate how much or how 
little it was wise to give to his audience, he continued: “and if the 
double do not succeed in get back to its physical body, that 
physical body would wake an imbecile--an idiot--or perhaps never wake 
at all.” 

maloney sat up and found his tongue. 

“you mean that if this fluid animal thing, or whatever it is, should be 
prevent get back, the man might never wake again?” he asked, with 
shake voice. 

“he might be dead,” reply the other calmly. the tremor of a positive 
sensation shiver in the air about us. 

“then isn’t that the best way to cure the fool--the brute----?” 
thunder the clergyman, half rising to his feet. 

“certainly it would be an easy and undiscoverable form of murder,” was 
the stern reply, spoken as calm as though it were a remark about the 
weather. 

maloney collapse visibly, and i gather the wood over the fire and 
coax up a blaze. 

“the greater part of the man’s life--of his vital forces--goes out with 
this double,” dr. silence resumed, after a moment’s consideration, “and 
a considerable portion of the actual material of his physical body. so 
the physical body that remains behind is depleted, not only of force, 
but of matter. you would see it small, shrunken, drop together, just 
like the body of a materialise medium at a séance. moreover, any mark 
or injury inflict upon this double will be found exactly reproduce 
by the phenomenon of repercussion upon the shrunken physical body lie 
in its trance----” 

“an injury inflict upon the one you say would be reproduce also on 
the other?” repeated maloney, his excitement grow again. 

“undoubtedly,” reply the other quietly; “for there exist all 
the time a continuous connection between the physical body and the 
double--a connection of matter, though of exceedingly attenuated, 
possibly of etheric, matter. the wound _travels_, so to speak, from one 
to the other, and if this connection were broken the result would be 
death.” 

“death,” repeated maloney to himself, “death!” he look anxious at 
our faces, his thought evidently beginning to clear. 

“and this solidity?” he ask presently, after a general pause; “this 
tear of tent and flesh; this howling, and the mark of paws? you 
mean that the double----?” 

“has sufficient material drawn from the deplete body to produce 
physical results? certainly!” the doctor took him up. “although to 
explain at this moment such problem as the passage of matter through 
matter would be as difficult as to explain how the thought of a mother 
can actually break the bone of the child unborn.” 

dr. silence pointed out to sea, and maloney, look wildly about 
him, turn with a violent start. i saw a canoe, with sangree in the 
stern-seat, slow coming into view round the farther point. his hat 
was off, and his tan face for the first time appear to me--to us 
all, i think--as though it were the face of some one else. he look 
like a wild man. then he stood up in the canoe to make a cast with the 
rod, and he look for all the world like an indian. i recall the 
expression of his face as i had seen it once or twice, notably on that 
occasion of the evening prayer, and an involuntary shudder ran down my 
spine. 

at that very instant he turn and saw us where we lay, and his face 
broke into a smile, so that his teeth show white in the sun. he 
look in his element, and exceedingly attractive. he call out 
something about his fish, and soon after pass out of sight into the 
lagoon. 

for a time none of us said a word. 

“and the cure?” venture maloney at length. 

“is not to quench this savage force,” reply dr. silence, “but to 
steer it better, and to provide other outlets. this is the solution 
of all these problem of accumulate force, for this force is the raw 
material of usefulness, and should be increase and cherished, not 
by separate it from the body by death, but by raise it to higher 
channels. the best and quickest cure of all,” he went on, speak very 
gently and with a hand upon the clergyman’s arm, “is to lead it towards 
its object, provided that object is not unalterable hostile--to let it 
find rest where----” 

he stop abruptly, and the eyes of the two men met in a single glance 
of comprehension. 

“joan?” maloney exclaimed, under his breath. 

“joan!” reply john silence. 

* * * * * 

we all went to bed early. the day had been unusually warm, and after 
sunset a curious hush descended on the island. nothing was audible but 
that faint, ghostly singing which is inseparable from a pine-wood even 
on the stillest day--a low, searching sound, as though the wind had 
hair and trail it o’er the world. 

with the sudden cool of the atmosphere a sea fog began to form. it 
appear in isolated patch over the water, and then these patch 
slid together and a white wall advanced upon us. not a breath of air 
stirred; the fir stood like flat metal outlines; the sea became as 
oil. the whole scene lay as though held motionless by some huge weight 
in the air; and the flame from our fire--the largest we had ever 
made--rose upwards, straight as a church steeple. 

as i follow the rest of our party tent-wards, have kick the 
ember of the fire into safety, the advance guard of the fog was 
creep slow among the trees, like white arms feeling their way. 
mingle with the smoke was the odour of moss and soil and bark, and 
the peculiar flavour of the baltic, half salt, half brackish, like the 
smell of an estuary at low water. 

it is difficult to say why it seem to me that this deep still 
masked an intense activity; perhaps in every mood lie the suggestion 
of its opposite, so that i became aware of the contrast of furious 
energy, for it was like moving through the deep pause before a 
thunderstorm, and i trod gently lest by break a twig or moving 
a stone i might set the whole scene into some sort of tumultuous 
movement. actually, no doubt, it was nothing more than a result of 
overstrung nerves. 

there was no more question of undress and go to bed than there 
was of undress and go to bathe. some sense in me was alert and 
expectant. i sat in my tent and waited. and at the end of half an hour 
or so my wait was justified, for the canvas sudden shivered, 
and some one trip over the ropes that held it to the earth. john 
silence came in. 

the effect of his quiet entry was singular and prophetic: it was just 
as though the energy lie behind all this still had pressed 
forward to the edge of action. this, no doubt, was merely the 
quicken of my own mind, and had no other justification; for the 
presence of john silence always suggest the near possibility of 
vigorous action, and, as a matter of fact, he came in with nothing more 
than a nod and a significant gesture. 

he sat down on a corner of my ground-sheet, and i pushed the blanket 
over so that he could cover his legs. he drew the flap of the tent 
after him and settled down, but hardly had he done so when the canvas 
shook a second time, and in blunder maloney. 

“sitting in the dark?” he said self-consciously, push his head 
inside, and hanging up his lantern on the ridge-pole nail. “i just 
look in for a smoke. i suppose----” 

he glance round, caught the eye of dr. silence, and stopped. he 
put his pipe back into his pocket and began to hum softly--that 
under-breath hum of a nondescript melody i knew so well and had 
come to hate. 

dr. silence lean forward, open the lantern and blew the light out. 
“speak low,” he said, “and don’t strike matches. listen for sound 
and movements about the camp, and be ready to follow me at a moment’s 
notice.” there was light enough to distinguish our face easily, and i 
saw maloney glance again hurried at both of us. 

“is the camp asleep?” the doctor ask presently, whispering. 

“sangree is,” reply the clergyman, in a voice equally low. “i can’t 
answer for the women; i think they’re sitting up.” 

“that’s for the best.” and then he added: “i wish the fog would thin a 
bit and let the moon through; later--we may want it.” 

“it is lift now, i think,” maloney whisper back. “it’s over the 
tops of the tree already.” 

i cannot say what it was in this commonplace exchange of remark 
that thrilled. probably maloney’s swift acquiesce in the doctor’s 
mood had something to do with it; for his quick obedience certainly 
impress me a good deal. but, even without that slight evidence, 
it was clear that each recognise the gravity of the occasion, and 
understood that sleep was impossible and sentry duty was the order of 
the night. 

“report to me,” repeated john silence once again, “the least sound, and 
do nothing precipitately.” 

he shift across to the mouth of the tent and raise the flap, 
fastening it against the pole so that he could see out. maloney stop 
hum and began to force the breath through his teeth with a kind 
of faint hissing, treat us to a medley of church hymn and popular 
song of the day. 

then the tent tremble as though some one had touched it. 

“that’s the wind rising,” whisper the clergyman, and pull the flap 
open as far as it would go. a waft of cold damp air enter and made us 
shiver, and with it came a sound of the sea as the first wave wash 
its way soft along the shores. 

“it’s got round to the north,” he added, and following his voice came 
a long-drawn whisper that rose from the whole island as the tree sent 
forth a sigh response. “the fog’ll move a bit now. i can make out a 
lane across the sea already.” 

“hush!” said dr. silence, for maloney’s voice had risen above a 
whisper, and we settled down again to another long period of watch 
and waiting, broken only by the occasional rubbing of shoulder against 
the canvas as we shift our positions, and the increase noise of 
wave on the outer coast-line of the island. and over all whirr the 
murmur of wind sweeping the tops of the tree like a great harp, and 
the faint tap on the tent as drops fell from the branch with a 
sharp ping sound. 

we had sat for something over an hour in this way, and maloney and i 
were finding it increasingly hard to keep awake, when sudden dr. 
silence rose to his feet and peer out. the next minute he was gone. 

relieved of the dominate presence, the clergyman thrust his face 
close into mine. “i don’t much care for this wait game,” he 
whispered, “but silence wouldn’t hear of my sitting up with the others; 
he said it would prevent anything happening if i did.” 

“he knows,” i answer shortly. 

“no doubt in the world about that,” he whisper back; “it’s this 
‘double’ business, as he call it, or else it’s obsession as the bible 
describe it. but it’s bad, whichever it is, and i’ve got my winchester 
outside ready cocked, and i brought this too.” he shove a pocket bible 
under my nose. at one time in his life it had been his inseparable 
companion. 

“one’s useless and the other’s dangerous,” i reply under my breath, 
conscious of a keen desire to laugh, and leave him to choose. “safety 
lie in following our leader----” 

“i’m not thinking of myself,” he interrupt sharply; “only, if 
anything happen to joan to-night i’m go to shoot first--and pray 
afterwards!” 

maloney put the book back into his hip-pocket, and peer out of the 
doorway. “what is he up to now, in the devil’s name, i wonder!” he 
added; “going round sangree’s tent and making gestures. how weird he 
looks disappear in and out of the fog.” 

“just trust him and wait,” i said quickly, for the doctor was already 
on his way back. “remember, he has the knowledge, and know what he’s 
about. i’ve been with him through worse case than this.” 

maloney move back as dr. silence darken the doorway and stoop to 
enter. 

“his sleep is very deep,” he whispered, seating himself by the door 
again. “he’s in a cataleptic condition, and the double may be release 
any minute now. but i’ve taken steps to imprison it in the tent, and it 
can’t get out till i permit it. be on the watch for sign of movement.” 
then he look hard at maloney. “but no violence, or shooting, 
remember, mr. maloney, unless you want a murder on your hands. anything 
done to the double acts by repercussion upon the physical body. you had 
better take out the cartridge at once.” 

his voice was stern. the clergyman went out, and i heard him empty 
the magazine of his rifle. when he return he sat near the door than 
before, and from that moment until we left the tent he never once took 
his eyes from the figure of dr. silence, silhouette there against sky 
and canvas. 

and, meanwhile, the wind came steady over the sea and open the mist 
into lane and clearings, driving it about like a living thing. 

it must have been well after midnight when a low boom sound drew my 
attention; but at first the sense of hearing was so strained that it 
was impossible exactly to locate it, and i imagine it was the thunder 
of big gun far out at sea carry to us by the rising wind. then 
maloney, catching hold of my arm and leaning forward, somehow brought 
the true relation, and i realise the next second that it was only a 
few feet away. 

“sangree’s tent,” he exclaim in a loud and startle whisper. 

i crane my head round the corner, but at first the effect of the 
fog was so confuse that every patch of white driving about before 
the wind look like a moving tent and it was some seconds before i 
discover the one patch that held steady. then i saw that it was 
shake all over, and the sides, flap as much as the tight of 
the ropes allowed, were the cause of the boom sound we had heard. 
something alive was tear frantic about inside, bang against 
the stretch canvas in a way that made me think of a great moth 
dashing against the wall and ceiling of a room. the tent bulge and 
rocked. 

“it’s try to get out, by jupiter!” mutter the clergyman, rising to 
his feet and turning to the side where the unload rifle lay. i sprang 
up too, hardly knowing what purpose was in my mind, but anxious to be 
prepared for anything. john silence, however, was before us both, and 
his figure slip past and block the doorway of the tent. and there 
was some quality in his voice next minute when he began to speak that 
brought our mind instantly to a state of calm obedience. 

“first--the women’s tent,” he said low, look sharp at maloney, 
“and if i need your help, i’ll call.” 

the clergyman need no second bidding. he dive past me and was out 
in a moment. he was labour evidently under intense excitement. i 
watch him pick his way silent over the slippery ground, give 
the moving tent a wide berth, and presently disappear among the 
floating shape of fog. 

dr. silence turn to me. “you heard those footstep about half an hour 
ago?” he ask significantly. 

“i heard nothing.” 

“they were extraordinarily soft--almost the soundless tread of a wild 
creature. but now, follow me closely,” he added, “for we must waste 
no time if i am to save this poor man from his affliction and lead 
his werewolf double to its rest. and, unless i am much mistaken”--he 
peer at me through the darkness, whisper with the utmost 
distinctness--“joan and sangree are absolutely made for one another. 
and i think she know it too--just as well as he does.” 

my head swam a little as i listened, but at the same time something 
clear in my brain and i saw that he was right. yet it was all so 
weird and incredible, so remote from the commonplace fact of life 
as commonplace people know them; and more than once it flash upon 
me that the whole scene--people, words, tents, and all the rest of 
it--were delusion create by the intense excitement of my own mind 
somehow, and that sudden the sea-fog would clear off and the world 
become normal again. 

the cold air from the sea stung our cheek sharp as we left the close 
atmosphere of the little crowded tent. the sigh of the trees, the 
wave break below on the rocks, and the lines and patch of mist 
driving about us seem to create the momentary illusion that the whole 
island had broken loose and was floating out to sea like a mighty raft. 

the doctor move just ahead of me, quick and silently; he was making 
straight for the canadian’s tent where the side still boom and shook 
as the creature of sinister life race and tore about impatient 
within. a little distance from the door he pause and held up a hand to 
stop me. we were, perhaps, a dozen feet away. 

“before i release it, you shall see for yourself,” he said, “that the 
reality of the werewolf is beyond all question. the matter of which 
it is compose is, of course, exceedingly attenuated, but you are 
partially clairvoyant--and even if it is not dense enough for normal 
sight you will see something.” 

he add a little more i could not catch. the fact was that the 
curious strong vibrate atmosphere surrounding his person somewhat 
confuse my senses. it was the result, of course, of his intense 
concentration of mind and forces, and pervade the entire camp and all 
the person in it. and as i watch the canvas shake and heard it boom 
and flap i heartily welcome it. for it was also protective. 

at the back of sangree’s tent stood a thin group of pine trees, but 
in front and at the side the ground was comparatively clear. the 
flap was wide open and any ordinary animal would have been out and 
away without the least trouble. dr. silence led me up to within a few 
feet, evidently careful not to advance beyond a certain limit, and then 
stoop down and signal to me to do the same. and look over his 
shoulder i saw the interior lit faint by the spectral light reflect 
from the fog, and the dim blot upon the balsam bough and blanket 
signify sangree; while over him, and round him, and up and down him, 
flew the dark mass of “something” on four legs, with pointed muzzle and 
sharp ear plainly visible against the tent sides, and the occasional 
gleam of fiery eyes and white fangs. 

i held my breath and kept utterly still, inward and outwardly, 
for fear, i suppose, that the creature would become conscious of my 
presence; but the distress i felt went far deep than the mere sense 
of personal safety, or the fact of watch something so incredible 
active and real. i became keen aware of the dreadful psychic calamity 
it involved. the realisation that sangree lay confine in that narrow 
space with this species of monstrous projection of himself--that he was 
wrap there in the cataleptic sleep, all unconscious that this thing 
was masquerade with his own life and energies--added a distressing 
touch of horror to the scene. in all the case of john silence--and 
they were many and often terrible--no other psychic affliction has 
ever, before or since, impress me so convincing with the pathetic 
impermanence of the human personality, with its fluid nature, and with 
the alarm possibility of its transformations. 

“come,” he whispered, after we had watch for some minutes the frantic 
effort to escape from the circle of thought and will that held it 
prisoner, “come a little farther away while i release it.” 

we move back a dozen yard or so. it was like a scene in some 
impossible play, or in some ghastly and oppressive nightmare from which 
i should presently awake to find the blanket all heap up upon my 
chest. 

by some method undoubted mental, but which, in my confusion and 
excitement, i fail to understand, the doctor accomplished his 
purpose, and the next minute i heard him say sharp under his breath, 
“it’s out! now, watch!” 

at this very moment a sudden gust from the sea blew aside the mist, so 
that a lane open to the sky, and the moon, ghastly and unnatural as 
the effect of stage limelight, drop down in a momentary gleam upon 
the door of sangree’s tent, and i perceive that something had move 
forward from the interior dark and stood clearly define upon the 
threshold. and, at the same moment, the tent cease its shudder and 
held still. 

there, in the doorway, stood an animal, with neck and muzzle thrust 
forward, its head poke into the night, its whole body poised in that 
attitude of intense rigidity that precede the spring into freedom, 
the running leap of attack. it seem to be about the size of a calf, 
lean than a mastiff, yet more squat than a wolf, and i can swear that 
i saw the fur ridge sharp upon its back. then its upper lip slow 
lifted, and i saw the white of its teeth. 

surely no human being ever stare as hard as i did in those next few 
minutes. yet, the hard i stare the clear appear the amazing and 
monstrous apparition. for, after all, it was sangree--and yet it was 
not sangree. it was the head and face of an animal, and yet it was the 
face of sangree: the face of a wild dog, a wolf, and yet his face. the 
eyes were sharper, narrower, more fiery, yet they were his eyes--his 
eyes run wild; the teeth were longer, whiter, more pointed--yet they 
were his teeth, his teeth grown cruel; the expression was flaming, 
terrible, exultant--yet it was his expression carry to the border of 
savagery--his expression as i had already surprise it more than once, 
only dominant now, fully release from human constraint, with the mad 
yearning of a hungry and importunate soul. it was the soul of sangree, 
the long suppressed, deep loving sangree, express in its single and 
intense desire--pure utterly and utterly wonderful. 

yet, at the same time, came the feeling that it was all an illusion. 
i sudden remember the extraordinary change the human face can 
undergo in circular insanity, when it change from melancholia to 
elation; and i recall the effect of hascheesh, which show the human 
countenance in the form of the bird or animal to which in character 
it most approximates; and for a moment i attribute this mingle of 
sangree’s face with a wolf to some kind of similar delusion of the 
senses. i was mad, deluded, dreaming! the excitement of the day, and 
this dim light of stars and bewilder mist combine to trick me. i 
had been amazing impose upon by some false wizardry of the senses. 
it was all absurd and fantastic; it would pass. 

and then, sound across this sea of mental confusion like a bell 
through a fog, came the voice of john silence bring me back to a 
consciousness of the reality of it all-- 

“sangree--in his double!” 

and when i look again more calmly, i plainly saw that it was indeed 
the face of the canadian, but his face turn animal, yet mingle with 
the brute expression a curious pathetic look like the soul seen 
sometimes in the yearning eyes of a dog,--the face of an animal shot 
with vivid streak of the human. 

the doctor call to him soft under his breath-- 

“sangree! sangree, you poor afflict creature! do you know me? can you 
understand what it is you’re do in your ‘body of desire’?” 

for the first time since its appearance the creature moved. its ear 
twitch and it shift the weight of its body on to the hind legs. 
then, lift its head and muzzle to the sky, it open its long jaws 
and gave vent to a dismal and prolonged howling. 

but, when i heard that howling rise to heaven, the breath caught and 
strangle in my throat and it seem that my heart miss a beat; for, 
though the sound was entire animal, it was at the same time entire 
human. but, more than that, it was the cry i had so often heard in the 
western states of america where the indian still fight and hunt and 
struggle--it was the cry of the redskin! 

“the indian blood!” whisper john silence, when i caught his arm for 
support; “the ancestral cry.” 

and that poignant, beseech cry, that broken human voice, mingle 
with the savage howl of the brute beast, pierce straight to my 
very heart and touched there something that no music, no voice, 
passionate or tender, of man, woman or child has ever stir before 
or since for one second into life. it echo away among the fog and 
the tree and lost itself somewhere out over the hidden sea. and some 
part of myself--something that was far more than the mere act of 
intense listening--went out with it, and for several minutes i lost 
consciousness of my surroundings and felt utterly absorb in the pain 
of another stricken fellow-creature. 

again the voice of john silence recall me to myself. 

“hark!” he said aloud. “hark!” 

his tone galvanise me afresh. we stood listen side by side. 

far across the island, faint sound through the tree and 
brushwood, came a similar, answer cry. shrill, yet wonderful 
musical, shake the heart with a singular wild sweet that defy 
description, we heard it rise and fall upon the night air. 

“it’s across the lagoon,” dr. silence cried, but this time in full 
tone that paid no tribute to caution. “it’s joan! she’s answer him!” 

again the wonderful cry rose and fell, and that same instant the animal 
lower its head, and, muzzle to earth, set off on a swift easy canter 
that took it off into the mist and out of our sight like a thing of 
wind and vision. 

the doctor made a quick dash to the door of sangree’s tent, and, 
following close at his heels, i peer in and caught a momentary 
glimpse of the small, shrunken body lie upon the branch but half 
cover by the blankets--the cage from which most of the life, and not 
a little of the actual corporeal substance, had escape into that other 
form of life and energy, the body of passion and desire. 

by another of those swift, incalculable process which at this stage 
of my apprenticeship i fail often to grasp, dr. silence reclose the 
circle about the tent and body. 

“now it cannot return till i permit it,” he said, and the next second 
was off at full speed into the woods, with myself close behind him. 
i had already had some experience of my companion’s ability to run 
swift through a dense wood, and i now had the further proof of his 
power almost to see in the dark. for, once we left the open space 
about the tents, the tree seem to absorb all the remain vestige 
of light, and i understood that special sensibility that is said to 
develop in the blind--the sense of obstacles. 

and twice as we ran we heard the sound of that dismal howling drawing 
near and near to the answer faint cry from the point of the 
island whither we were going. 

then, suddenly, the tree fell away, and we emerged, hot and 
breathless, upon the rocky point where the granite slab ran bare into 
the sea. it was like passing into the clear of open day. and there, 
sharp define against sea and sky, stood the figure of a human being. 
it was joan. 

i at once saw that there was something about her appearance that was 
singular and unusual, but it was only when we had move quite close 
that i recognise what cause it. for while the lip wore a smile that 
lit the whole face with a happiness i had never seen there before, the 
eyes themselves were fixed in a steady, sightless stare as though they 
were lifeless and made of glass. 

i made an impulsive forward movement, but dr. silence instantly drag 
me back. 

“no,” he cried, “don’t wake her!” 

“what do you mean?” i reply aloud, struggle in his grasp. 

“she’s asleep. it’s somnambulistic. the shock might injure her 
permanently.” 

i turn and peer close into his face. he was absolutely calm. i 
began to understand a little more, catching, i suppose, something of 
his strong thinking. 

“walking in her sleep, you mean?” 

he nodded. “she’s on her way to meet him. from the very beginning he 
must have drawn her--irresistibly.” 

“but the torn tent and the wound flesh?” 

“when she did not sleep deep enough to enter the somnambulistic trance 
he miss her--he went instinctive and in all innocence to seek her 
out--with the result, of course, that she woke and was terrified----” 

“then in their heart of heart they love?” i ask finally. 

john silence smile his inscrutable smile: “profoundly,” he answered, 
“and as simply as only primitive soul can love. if only they both come 
to realise it in their normal waking states his double will cease these 
nocturnal excursions. he will be cured, and at rest.” 

the words had hardly left his lip when there was a sound of rustling 
branch on our left, and the very next instant the dense brushwood 
part where it was darkest and out rush the swift form of an animal 
at full gallop. the noise of feet was scarcely audible, but in that 
utter still i heard the heavy pant breath and caught the swish 
of the low bush against its sides. it went straight towards joan--and 
as it went the girl lift her head and turn to meet it. and the same 
instant a canoe that had been creep silent and unobserved round 
the inner shore of the lagoon, emerge from the shadow and define 
itself upon the water with a figure at the middle thwart. it was 
maloney. 

it was only afterwards i realise that we were invisible to him where 
we stood against the dark background of trees; the figures of joan and 
the animal he saw plainly, but not dr. silence and myself standing just 
beyond them. he stood up in the canoe and pointed with his right arm. i 
saw something gleam in his hand. 

“stand aside, joan girl, or you’ll get hit,” he shouted, his voice 
ring horrible through the deep stillness, and the same instant a 
pistol-shot cracked out with a burst of flame and smoke, and the figure 
of the animal, with one tremendous leap into the air, fell back in the 
shadow and disappear like a shape of night and fog. instantly, then, 
joan open her eyes, look in a daze fashion about her, and pressing 
both hand against her heart, fell with a sharp cry into my arms that 
were just in time to catch her. 

and an answer cry sound across the lagoon--thin, wailing, piteous. 
it came from sangree’s tent. 

“fool!” cry dr. silence, “you’ve wound him!” and before we could 
move or realise quite what it meant, he was in the canoe and half-way 
across the lagoon. 

some kind of similar abuse came in a torrent from my lip too--though 
i cannot remember the actual words--as i cursed the man for his 
disobedience and try to make the girl comfortable on the ground. but 
the clergyman was more practical. he was spread his coat over her 
and dashing water on her face. 

“it’s not joan i’ve kill at any rate,” i heard him mutter as she 
turn and open her eyes and smile faint up in his face. “i swear 
the bullet went straight.” 

joan stare at him; she was still daze and bewildered, and still 
imagine herself with the companion of her trance. the strange lucid 
of the somnambulist still hung over her brain and mind, though 
outwardly she appear trouble and confused. 

“where has he gone to? he disappear so suddenly, crying that he was 
hurt,” she asked, look at her father as though she did not recognise 
him. “and if they’ve done anything to him--they have done it to me 
too--for he is more to me than----” 

her words grew vague and vague as she return slow to her normal 
waking state, and now she stop altogether, as though sudden aware 
that she had been surprise into telling secrets. but all the way back, 
as we carry her careful through the trees, the girl smile and 
murmur sangree’s name and ask if he was injured, until it finally 
became clear to me that the wild soul of the one had call to the 
wild soul of the other and in the secret depths of their being the 
call had been heard and understood. john silence was right. in the 
abyss of her heart, too deep at first for recognition, the girl love 
him, and had love him from the very beginning. once her normal waking 
consciousness recognise the fact they would leap together like twin 
flames, and his affliction would be at an end; his intense desire would 
be satisfied; he would be cured. 

and in sangree’s tent dr. silence and i sat up for the remainder of the 
night--this wonderful and haunt night that had shown us such strange 
glimpse of a new heaven and a new hell--for the canada toss upon 
his balsam bough with high fever in his blood, and upon each cheek a 
dark and curious contusion showed, throb with severe pain although
