the skin was not broken and there was no outward and visible sign of 
blood. 

“maloney shot straight, you see,” whisper dr. silence to me after the 
clergyman had gone to his tent, and had put joan to sleep beside her 
mother, who, by the way, had never once awakened. “the bullet must have 
pass clean through the face, for both cheek are stained. he’ll wear 
these mark all his life--smaller, but always there. they’re the most 
curious scar in the world, these scar transfer by repercussion 
from an injure double. they’ll remain visible until just before his 
death, and then with the withdrawal of the subtle body they will 
disappear finally.” 

his words mingle in my daze mind with the sigh of the trouble 
sleeper and the crying of the wind about the tent. nothing seem to 
paralyse my powers of realisation so much as these twin stain of 
mysterious significance upon the face before me. 

it was odd, too, how speedy and easily the camp resigned itself 
again to sleep and quietness, as though a stage curtain had sudden 
drop down upon the action and conceal it; and nothing contribute 
so vivid to the feeling that i had been a spectator of some kind of 
visionary drama as the dramatic nature of the change in the girl’s 
attitude. 

yet, as a matter of fact, the change had not been so sudden and 
revolutionary as appeared. underneath, in those remote regions 
of consciousness where the emotions, unknown to their owners, do 
secret mature, and owe thence their abrupt revelation to some abrupt 
psychological climax, there can be no doubt that joan’s love for the 
canada had been grow steady and irresistible all the time. it 
had now rush to the surface so that she recognise it; that was all. 

and it has always seem to me that the presence of john silence, 
so potent, so quiet efficacious, produce an effect, if one may 
say so, of a psychic forcing-house, and hasten incalculable the 
bring together of these two “wild” lovers. in that sudden awakening 
had occur the very psychological climax require to reveal the 
passionate emotion accumulate below. the deep knowledge had leap 
across and transfer itself to her ordinary consciousness, and in 
that shock the collision of the personalities had shaken them to the 
depths and shown her the truth beyond all possibility of doubt. 

“he’s sleep quiet now,” the doctor said, interrupt my 
reflections. “if you will watch alone for a bit i’ll go to maloney’s 
tent and help him to arrange his thoughts.” he smile in anticipation 
of that “arrangement.” “he’ll never quite understand how a wound on the 
double can transfer itself to the physical body, but at least i can 
persuade him that the less he talks and ‘explains’ tomorrow, the soon 
the forces will run their natural course now to peace and quietness.” 

he went away softly, and with the removal of his presence sangree, 
sleep heavily, turn over and groan with the pain of his broken 
head. 

and it was in the still hour just before the dawn, when all the island 
were hushed, the wind and sea still dreaming, and the stars visible 
through clearing mists, that a figure crept silent over the ridge and 
reach the door of the tent where i doze beside the sufferer, before 
i was aware of its presence. the flap was cautious lift a few 
inch and in looked--joan. 

that same instant sangree woke and sat up on his bed of branches. he 
recognise her before i could say a word, and utter a low cry. it was 
pain and joy mingled, and this time all human. and the girl too was no 
long walking in her sleep, but fully aware of what she was doing. i 
was only just able to prevent him spring from his blankets. 

“joan, joan!” he cried, and in a flash she answer him, “i’m here--i’m 
with you always now,” and had pushed past me into the tent and flung 
herself upon his breast. 

“i knew you would come to me in the end,” i heard him whisper. 

“it was all too big for me to understand at first,” she murmured, “and 
for a long time i was frightened----” 

“but not now!” he cry louder; “you don’t feel afraid now of--of 
anything that’s in me----” 

“i fear nothing,” she cried, “nothing, nothing!” 

i led her outside again. she look steady into my face with eyes 
shining and her whole being transformed. in some intuitive way, 
survive probably from the somnambulism, she knew or guess as much 
as i knew. 

“you must talk tomorrow with john silence,” i said gently, leading her 
towards her own tent. “he understand everything.” 

i left her at the door, and as i went back soft to take up my place 
of sentry again with the canadian, i saw the first streak of dawn 
lighting up the far rim of the sea behind the distant islands. 

and, as though to emphasise the eternal close of comedy to tragedy, 
two small detail rose out of the scene and impress me so vivid 
that i remember them to this very day. for in the tent where i had 
just left joan, all aquiver with her new happiness, there rose plainly 
to my ear the grotesque sound of the bo’sun’s mate heavy snoring, 
oblivious of all things in heaven or hell; and from maloney’s tent, so 
still was the night, where i look across and saw the lantern’s glow, 
there came to me, through the trees, the monotonous rising and fall 
of a human voice that was beyond question the sound of a man pray to 
his god.
